text:
Awesome good! Great departure from traditional pizza toppings and sauce. I used half of a 3 c. flour recipe for bread machine pizza dough rather than the the prepared, refrigerated crust. For added flavor, I seasoned the chicken with salt,pepper,and a little garlic powder and sauteed them in olive oil.  I lightly brushed the crust with olive oil before topping with the other ingredients, added sliced, fresh mushrooms, and drizzled about 1 T. of olive oil over the top before baking. This was a fun twist on the traditional pie. I enjoyed making it and enjoyed eating it even more!

text:
I was excited to try this recipe as we all use Ranch dressing as a "dip" for our regular pizza.  It was so good and a very nice change to regular pizza!  I think the key here is: 1)Use a good thick ranch dressing, and rather than measuring it, I just spread it on like I would pizza sauce; 2) A thick pizza crust is key, couldn't see this on a thin crust at all; 3) Make sure your chicken is seasoned how you like it or it will be bland.  Another tip is use lots of chicken, mine seemed to disappear when the cheese melted, so I'm going to use more next time.  I used the canned tomatoes that were tiny chopped and seasoned and it worked great.  I added chopped bacon pieces to half and it was good also.  I think I'll try salsa next time.  I've also made this with the chicken sauteed in BBQ sauce first, which was a nice change but not as good as the original.

text:
This was excellent! I made several changes, like I usually do, to suit my family's tastes. I used a combo of boneless, skinless thighs & breasts, which I marinated for 5 hours with a vidalia onion vinaigrette, minced garlic and seasoned salt & pepper. I grilled the chicken then cooled and chopped into bite size pieces.  I used Pillsbury's Thin Crust refrigerated pizza crust. Before pre-baking for 8 minutes at 400 degrees (425 is too high), I sprayed the crust with olive oil Pam and sprinkled garlic powder over it. I used a can of seasoned diced tomatoes, drained, a can of portabella sliced mushrooms, drained, the green onions, a small can of sliced black olives, drained, and a 1/2 pkg. of Hormel real bacon bits. I used a thick ranch jar dressing (Litehouse, Jimmy's or Marie's works well), but didn't measure, just spread a layer on the pre-baked crust. I did layer the cheeses and other ingredients, in addition to my own, as the recipe states, then baked for an additional 17 minutes at 400 degrees instead of 425. I let it stand for 7 minutes to set the toppings and prevent them from sliding off while slicing the pizza.  Everyone LOVED this pizza and it I will be making it a regular rotation in my menu planning.

text:
I already make this however we barbeque ours. You can buy special pans (i bought mine at Walmart) with little round holes in the bottom for this purpose. You could probably make your own with cheap tin pans from the dollar store by making some holes in the bottom. We try all kinds of variations. A couple of hits are mixing some Rene's Ceasar dressing or Spicy Thialand (M&M's) with tomatoe sauce on the crust. This makes a Chicken Ceasar Pizza or a Spicy Chicken Thai Pizza. Be careful if you do make it on the BBQ as it takes less than 13 minutes. Try to keep your heat to under 400 as well. We use any crust and have used the refridgerator dough as suggested here with great results. Even on the BBQ. This  the best tasteing pizza ever (double delish on the BBQ) and is always a hit at my house.

I thought this tasted pretty good. I was looking for a pizza similar to the bbq chicken pizza, but without the spiceness. I used low fat cheeses and ranch dressing and it did not seem to be a problem. To cook the chicken more easily I just boiled one large chicken breast in some water with a packet of no-sodium chicken broth powder and then shredded it. text:
Ok so I was a little bit hesitant about this recipe because I'm not a huge ranch fan...hubby is though-he loves to dip his pizza in ranch, so when I saw this recipe I thought he'd love it. Well, let me tell you we BOTH devoured this!! It was so yummy! I didn't really measure out the ranch, I just used enough to cover the pizza crust--and it almost seemed like an alfredo sauce...it was delicious!  The recipe as is I would give 4 stars. I made a couple changes based on others' reviews that made it 5 stars! First, I used a boboli crustinstead of refridgerated and chives instead of green onions because that's what I happened to have on hand. Second, I seasoned my chicken with fresh garlic and italian seasoning. I used fresh, diced tomatoes (again, what I had on hand). And I added some crumbled bacon on top...can't wait to have this again! The recipe as-is is wonderful, but season your chicken and add some bacon and my-oh-my is it good!

My husband and I love this pizza!  It is very quick and easy to make.  I save more time if I use the recipe-ready pre-cooked and cut chicken from Perdue or Tyson, rather than cooking and cutting up the chicken myself.  

Also, we found that 1/2 cup of ranch dressing is a little too much so I suggest decreasing it to maybe 1/4.  I also added minced garlic and fresh basil leaves.  

It doesn't make 8 servings.  My husband and I split an entire pizza in one sitting.

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
My husband said that the only thing that could make this pizza better would be if the crust hadn't been so well done! That was my fault, of course, for leaving it in the oven too long. But even so, we loved this pizza. It was a wonderful change of pace from your traditional pizza with red sauce. I read most of the reviews and did make a few changes accordingly. 1) Some people said that the ranch made it greasy, so I used way less dressing than called for and then served it with more to dip in, which worked out perfectly. 2) Many people commented that the recipe as is was a bit bland, so when I cooked the chicken (which I cut into small pieces beforehand), I added one very large clove of garlic (minced), salt, and a generous amount of freshly ground black pepper. Then when I assembled the pizza, I sprinkled pizza seasoning (came with my spice rack--probably has basil, oregano, thyme, etc) on top of the chicken, tomatoes, and onions. 3) I used a colby-jack blend instead of the cheddar and mozarella. 4) I sprinkled the baking sheet with cornmeal, and decreased the temp to 400. I baked the crust alone for 6 1/2 minutes, then the pizza for about 15, which was obviously a little long. With these changes, the pizza turned out incredible and I will definitely make it again...and hopefully not burn it!

text:
This was a crowd pleaser.  Everyone here really liked it.  I made a few changes, but not many -- I added a couple of tablespoons of chopped fresh herbs; rosemary, oregano and cilantro.  Those were sprinkled on top of the ranch dressing.  I marinated my chicken for about an hour in Seven Seas Italian Dressing mixed 2 to 1 with lemon juice.  I used some of the spices along with dried basil and garlic while cooking the chicken.  I used prebaked, super thin pizza crusts and cut way down on the baking time.  I sprinkled my diced tomatoes with dried basil, oregano and garlic powder and let them sit that way for a while before use, just to give them a little extra flavor.
Excellent, excellent, excellent.  I may never make plain pizza again!!!!!

text:
My husband and I love this pizza - probably me more than him. I don't really measure out my ingredients, because this recipe is so much about personal taste, and it's very forgiving! I took another cook's suggestion and seasoned my cooking chicken with montreal steak seasoning (what an awesome flavor!) and then, when the chicken was done, I added barbeque sauce into the pan which was still at a pretty high heat. I let the chicken simmer in that for about a minute, just enough to reduce the bbq sauce, then put the chicken pieces on top of the ranch and cheese layer. We left off the tomatoes and onions and instead just added the last layer of cheece. Before I put it in the oven I sprinkled the top of the pizza with more bbq sauce. I also noticed people having trouble with the crust - I followed the directions on the can of Pilsbury pizza crust I used, baking the crust alone for 8 minutes, adding toppings, and then baking it for 10 more minutes. It turned out perfectly! DELICIOUS!

I also add some thinly sliced red onion, for extra flavor..When pre-baking the crust, be sure that the edges don't get over-done - I reduced the heat during this phase, the second time I made it - and also brushed the dough with garlic olive oil, for extra flavor...

text:
Really good and easy to make!! I used Boboli pizza crust. I deviated slightly from the steps. I shredded the chicken as it cooked which decreased the cooking time. While it cooked, I salted it and added garlic powder. After I spread the ranch dressing on the crust, I sprinkled dried oregano to give it an authentic pizza taste. Since I didn't have tomatoes or green onions, I added chopped shitake mushrooms, which definitely added to the gourmet-ness of the pizza. This pizza was truly tasty and it's the ranch dressing that is the differentiator. When you bite into it the zangy taste of the dressing pops through. So be sure you like ranch dressing before using this recipe. Will definitely make again!

All I can say is, Wow. I had one leftover slice and brought it to another friend to try the next day, and even reheated in the microwave he said it was really good.

text:
I have to give this 4 stars because I changed it so much but it tasted so good it was really 5 stars.  I used two Boboli style pizza crusts.  Blue cheese dressing instead of ranch.  Divided a can of diced tomatoes with basil, garlic & oregano between the two pizzas.  I minced two cloves of garlic then added them to a heated pan with extra virgin olive oil.  I took a package of chicken thighs trimmed the fat and cut them into bite sized pieces sprinkled them with California garlic salt and a dash of cayenne pepper and added them to the heated pan of olive oil and minced garlic & dried minced onions until the chicken was almost cooked through.  I added the chicken to the pizzas.  Topped them with a combination of mozzarella & cheddar cheese.  Finished them off with sliced black olives.  Yummy!

text:
I made this the other night and was very pleased with the outcome. After reading some of the reviews, I decided to saute the chicken in extra virgin olive oil with minced garlic, salt & pepper and I topped the pizza with dried basil flakes. I also noticed that the crust was golden brown after the 7 minutes so I lowered the heat to 400 degrees and baked the pizza for 15 min. instead of 20 - 25 min. It came out perfect. What's really great about this recipe is that you can add extra veggies or different meats, whatever you like.

text:
I am not exactly sure how many stars to give this recipe.  I think that it would have been good if it wouldn't have been so BURNED!!!  I baked the crust on a baking sheet.  After the initial 7 minutes of pre-baking it had a nice, light, golden brown color to it.  I piled it with toppings, put it back in the oven for only 19 or 20 minutes (recipe said 20-25) and it was smoking!  The top actually turned out pretty well, but the ENTIRE bottom of the crust was burned!  And I mean completely black burned!  So, I think that a lower temp (maybe 400 instead of 425) might be the answer.  I am going to give it one more try, as the toppings seemed a good combination.....just very disappointed about the burned crust.  So, watch this pizza in the oven very carefully, and you may want to think about turning down the temp for the final baking.

text:
I had pre-made dough and supermarket rotisserie chicken on hand, so this looked like a great Saturday afternoon lunch, and it was! My husband loved it (comparing it to the actual gourmet pizza place in town). Using ingredients I had on hand in combination with tips provided by other reviewers, I made the following modifications: used Light Ranch dressing, seasoned the cooked chicken with Grill Mates Montreal Chicken Seasoning, used a drained 14.5 oz can of Hunts diced Oregan/Rosemary tomatoes, used shallots in place of the green onions, and added a sprinkle of Baco-Bits on top before popping it into the oven. Followed the baking instructions and layering of ingredients exactly from the original recipe. What a tasty pizza. Flavorful, firm, filling, and very pretty to look at. This is a keeper.

I make my own pizza dough, but next time will make thicker dough, sprinkled with corn meal on the bottom..  Then I sprinkled freshly grated Parmesan cheese on the dough and baked for 5 minutes.  Pulling out the pre-baked dough,  I added a tablespoon of pesto to my fresh tomatoes after I chopped them.  Using garlic butter,1 I sauteed the chicken and onions until done.  I used 1/4 cup + 2 tablespoons of ranch dressing,  Instead of Mozzarella cheese, I used Mexican blend for all the cheese (all I had on hand)...Excellent flavor!  This definitely goes into my Recipe Box.  Oh!  I baked mine @ 500 degrees...better crust that way.

I use canned diced tomatoes with garlic and basil to give it a little more flavor and add fresh bacon. You can use whatever kind of cheese you have at home; I usually use colby jack. Putting the cheese on top helps to keep all the toppings from falling off. Because I don't like traditional pizza sauce, this is my kind of pizza, and I everyone I make it for loves it!

This wasn't really what I was expecting. I was hoping it would taste like the Walmart Great Value Bacon Cheddar Ranch pizza. Its not even close. That frozen Pizza is the BEST pizza I've ever had. On the other hand, this pizza isn't bad. The only portion of the recipe I followed was the time (which is too much) and the amount of cheese & ranch. I threw on a lot of bacon, some cooked onions, and some frozen precooked & seasoned chicken. My first bite I was kinda disgusted. But once it cooled off a little it was better. Definitely something different. A little weird flavor. Probably not a favorite of mine. But not horrible. I think my other issue was the dough never rose (despite the water being the right temp and the yeast being good). As for the cooktime, I precooked my own dough 7 minutes, took it out put the cheese and ranch on, and popped it back in for 14 minutes. It was done. Maybe a little over done. Then I put all the cooked stuff on top and put it in a turned off oven for a couple minutes. I'll try it again with a different dough. I sure wish I could figure out what Walmart uses for Ranch on their pizza.

text:
Great pizza! I needed a quick dinner tonight and this was just the ticket :) My fiance and I had to grocery shop (we didn't get around to it this past weekend), so I knew that I couldn't spend a lot of time in the kitchen. On our shopping trip to the local Italian market, I picked up Tyson oven roasted chicken chunks (5 oz. pkg.) and fresh pizza dough to speed prep even further. When I got home, all I had to do was chop the veggies and voila! I followed Lessalee's directions almost exactly. My only change was seasoning my chicken with a bit of garlic powder (we like our garlic!). Next time, I will be sure to increase the onion to 1/2 c. (1/4 c. wasn't enough, IMHO) and add some fresh (or Hormel real pieces) of bacon. I will also most definitely pre-bake my crust (7 minutes was perfect) and then bake for 22.5 minutes as I did this time. I have found that if I do not pre-bake, the Caputo's crust I usually purchase ends up soggy. This time it was perfectly crisp (just how we prefer it). Thanks for sharing such a great recipe, Lesalee!!! My fiance didn't care for this (he doesn't care for ranch), but I sure did! I'll just have to make a smaller pizza for myself next time :)

I can't believe I made this pizza myself, it tasted so good! I added a few additions: cornmeal at the bottom of the dough (for texture), bacon, seasoned the chicken, used spicy ranch instead of regular ranch, canned tomoatoes instead of regular tomatoes and finally, after it came out of the oven I topped it with fresh chopped cilantro! What's great about this recipe is that it is very versatile and you can change it or add to it whatever you like.
